## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of a chemical species concentration as a function of time and current concentration. The rate law dA/dt = f(A, t) typically follows power-law, rational, or composite forms depending on the reaction mechanism.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular reactions)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reactions)
- Fractional-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical fractional reaction order)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order forward and reverse with constant product)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reactions)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type rate law)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis with finite capacity)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-modulated first-order kinetics)
- Competitive pathway: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) + c2 * A (combined saturation and linear terms)
- Power-law with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration-only dependence (no explicit time) → autonomous ODE rate law, most common in elementary reaction mechanisms
- Rational dependence on A (numerator/denominator polynomials in A) → suggests multi-step mechanism with quasi-steady-state intermediates
- Integer power of concentration → elementary reaction with molecularity equal to the power
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or reversible reaction where product concentration is conserved (A + B = const)
- Square root or fractional power of A → dissociative equilibrium or surface reaction mechanism (e.g., A**0.5 from dissociation)
- Negative rate values (dA_dt < 0) with magnitude increasing with A → consumption reaction where A is a reactant
- Rate approaching constant at high A → zero-order regime from enzyme saturation or surface site saturation
- Explicit time dependence in rate → non-autonomous system suggesting external forcing, photolysis, or temperature ramp
- Sum of terms with different powers of A → parallel reaction pathways with different molecularities
